Federal Forfeitures Initiated ............................................................................................. 277 
Federal Forfeitures Completed ......................................................................................... 279 Asset forfeiture, as established under various state and federal statutes, is intended 
to disrupt criminal activities through the seizure and forfeiture of the instruments or 
proceeds of crime. 
Pursuant to California Health and Safety Code Section 11495, the California Department 
of Justice (DOJ) publishes an annual report providing information on forfeiture actions during the preceding calendar year. This 26th annual report covers the 2020 calendar year. The DOJ received federal seizure and forfeiture information from 35 out of approximately 400 state and local law enforcement agencies, and state seizure and forfeiture information from 45 out of 58 district attorneys’ ofces. 
Health and Safety Code Section 1 1 495 
11495(a) The funds received by the law enforcement agencies under section 11489 
shall be deposited into an account maintained by the Controller, county auditor, or city treasurer. These funds shall be distributed to the law enforcement agencies at their request. The Controller, auditor, or treasurer shall maintain a record of these disbursements which records shall be open to public inspection, subject to the privileges contained in sections 1040, 1041, and 1042 of the Evidence Code. 
(b) Upon request of the governing body of the jurisdiction in which the distributions are 
made, the Controller, auditor, or treasurer shall conduct an audit of these funds and their use. In the case of the state, the governing body shall be the Legislature. 
(c) Each year, the Attorney General shall publish a report which sets forth the following 
information for the state, each county, each city, and each city and county:  
(1) The number of forfeiture actions initiated and administered by state or local 
agencies under California law, the number of cases adopted by the federal government, and the number of cases initiated by a joint federal-state action that were prosecuted under federal law. 
(2) The number of cases and the administrative number or court docket number of 
each case for which forfeiture was ordered or declared. 
(3) The number of suspects charged with a controlled substance violation. 
1  
continued 
(4) The number of alleged criminal ofenses that were under federal or state law. 
(5) The disposition of cases, including no charge, dropped charges, acquittal, plea 
agreement, jury conviction, or other. 
(6) The value of the assets forfeited. 
(7) The recipients of the forfeited assets, the amounts received, and the date of 
the disbursement. 
(d) The Attorney General shall develop administrative guidelines for the collection and 
publication of the information required in subdivision (c). 
(e) The Attorney General’s report shall cover the calendar year and shall be made no 
later than July 1 of each year beginning with the year after the enactment of this law. 
2 Statistics were solicited from California’s district attorneys’ ofces and law enforcement 
agencies. Although the DOJ is required to prepare this report, local agencies are not statutorily mandated to provide their data to the DOJ for inclusion. The 2020 report refects the responses that were received from 45 district attorneys and 35 state and local law enforcement agencies. In California, there are 58 district attorneys and approximately 400 law enforcement agencies. Based on the data received by the Department of Justice, the following highlights the fndings in this report: 
 •  A total of 3,039 state forfeiture proceedings were initiated in 2020 (Table 1). 
 •  A total of 932 federal forfeiture sharing requests were submitted in 2020 (Table 4). 
 •  A total of 1,938 state forfeiture cases were completed during 2020, which included   
  cases initiated in 2020 and prior years. The total value of the disbursed assets is   
  $25,739,328.57 (Table 2). 
 •  A total of 583 joint federal asset forfeiture cases in which state or local law    
  enforcement participated were completed and disbursed during 2020. The total value  
  of the federal equitable sharing funds received is $16,832,292.44 (Table 5). 
 •  Inyo County reported no state forfeiture cases initiated or completed in 2020 (Table 3). 
 •  The following ffteen counties did not participate in providing data for this report:   
  Alpine, Calaveras, Del Norte, Mariposa, Merced, Mono, Nevada, San Benito,  
  San Francisco, San Luis Obispo, Sierra, Siskiyou, Sutter, Yolo and Yuba. 
 •  A total of 35 state and local law enforcement agencies participated in this report,   
  twelve of which reported no federal equitable sharing funds received (Table 6).

To comply with the requirements of Health and Safety Code section 11495, the DOJ 
reached out to all California district attorneys, the ofcials conducting state forfeiture 
proceedings, to request that they provide the DOJ with the required information for each state forfeiture action conducted during the reporting period. Although the DOJ is required to prepare this report, local agencies are not statutorily mandated to provide their data to the DOJ for inclusion. 
Information regarding federal equitable sharing sought and received by California law 
enforcement agencies through joint investigations can only be obtained directly from the participating agencies. This is the third report to include federal forfeiture data and the third time agencies other than district attorneys’ ofces have been called upon to participate. 
This report provides the information required by Health and Safety Code section 11495 
on all forfeitures initiated during calendar year 2020. For state forfeitures completed and federal distributions received during calendar year 2020, detailed information is provided. 
Pursuant to Health and Safety Code section 11489, state asset forfeiture proceeds are 
distributed as follows: 
• One percent to a private, nonproft organization composed of local prosecutors for the exclusive purpose of providing a statewide program of education and training for prosecutors and law enforcement in the ethics and proper use of State asset forfeiture laws. 
• Ten percent to the prosecutorial agency that processes the forfeiture action.  
• Twenty-four percent to the State General Fund. 
• Sixty-fve percent to the state and/or local law enforcement agencies that participated in the seizure of the assets, distributed in a manner that refects the proportionate contribution of each agency. Fifteen percent
1 of the funds distributed to law 
enforcement must be deposited in a special fund which is maintained by a council made up of local government entities. This fund shall be used for the sole purpose of funding programs designed to combat drug abuse and divert gang activity. 
1 Some counties have reported the deposit of 1 5 percent of their share to a special fund while 
others have not, nor are they required to.

continued 
Federal asset forfeiture proceeds received by a state or local law enforcement agency may 
be utilized for allowable law enforcement purposes as defned in the Federal Guide to Equitable Sharing. Health and Safety Code section 11471.2 prohibits state and local law enforcement agencies from seeking federal adoption of specifed asset seizures. It also prohibits acceptance of certain federal equitable sharing distributions when the asset seized is real property or less than $40,000 in cash or other negotiable instruments, unless the underlying criminal case has resulted in a conviction. When such prohibited seizures are ordered forfeited, the participating California agency must decline or return the distribution. In those cases, the entire forfeited amount is retained by the federal agency.

•  Table 2 provides summary information on asset forfeiture actions completed   
 pursuant to California law during 2020. This includes disbursement information on  
 cases initiated in 2020 and prior years (Page 14). 
•  Table 3 is the most extensive section within this report and provides detailed   
 information on each asset forfeiture case that was completed pursuant to state law  
 during 2020 (Page 16). 
•  Table 5 provides summary information on federal asset forfeitures received by state  
 and local law enforcement agencies as part of a joint asset forfeiture case in 2020,  
 including cases initiated in 2020 and prior years (Page 279).

 equitable sharing funds were disbursed to California law enforcement agencies   
 during 2020 (Page 280). 
•  Cases for which only a partial distribution was made during 2020 are not listed in  
 Tables 3 or 6, as they are considered still pending. They will be reported once they  
 are fully distributed.

•  Tables 4, 5, and 6 refect data reported by law enforcement agencies.
